#### 37\. Threats Against Company, Cancelation, Termination of Goods and Services

The company aixeno inc., conducting its software publishing business through the website [https://aixeno.com](https://aixeno.com/ "click or tap to go to aixeno.com - https://aixeno.com") may receive threats of any kind during the normal course of business.  
  
"The company" means the corporation aixeno inc., and includes (without limitation) its directors, officers, managers, employees, agents, vendors, consumers, customers, end-users, affiliates, successors, assigns, partners, shareholders, or any other related and interested parties of the company.  
  
A threat against the company is considered to be any threat of any kind, from anywhere in the world, which is a communication in any form or format (verbal, written, electronic, digital, analog or otherwise) made against the company (directly or indirectly) by any consumer, end-user, any bot, robot, chatbot, or any human person or other entity that is intended in any way to negatively affect the company by: using words threatening violence and/or destruction, inciting others to commit crimes or violence or destruction, causing harm of any kind, withhold something of value, interfere with or disrupt anything related to the company's normal course of business, cause any risk of financial loss, cause legal jeopardy including a false police report and/or a frivolous lawsuit, doxxing, swatting, false comments and/or malicious comments using threatening words or phrases, defamation or libel or slander, disparagement or other reputational harm to the good business reputation of the company or its digital solutions and digital technologies, commission of any crimes against the company, commission of any torts against the company, impersonate the company, or attempts to commit any fraudulent activities against the company. A threat against the company may also take the form of publishing a threat against the company onto and through any posting of threatening information on any news website, social media platform or website, in emails, text messages, any bot, robot, chatbot, or any other form of media and communication technology. Threats may be started from any location on the internet or from any geographic location in the world.  
  
According to applicable laws the company aixeno inc. has the lawful right(s) to respond to any threats received, by immediately terminating, rescinding, disclaiming, denying, and/or canceling any present or future:

* a.   -  access to or use of company website(s) owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* b.   -  use of digital solutions and digital technologies owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* c.   -  license(s) issued by or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* d.   -  digital services owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* e.   -  provision of service(s) owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* f.   -  account(s) owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* g.   -  subscription(s) issued by or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* h.   -  sale(s) initiated by or in progress with aixeno inc.;
* i.   -  transaction(s) that in any way involve aixeno inc.;
* j.   -  approval(s) that in any way involve or require a decision by aixeno inc.;
* k.   -  authorization(s) that in any way involve or require a decision by aixeno inc.;
* l.   -  payment(s) that in any way involve transactions with or by aixeno inc.;
* m.   -  discount(s) that are within the exclusive and sole discretion of aixeno inc.;
* n.   -  refund(s) discount(s) that are within the exclusive and sole discretion of aixeno inc.;
* o.   -  data owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;

* q.   -  access to or entry upon any company property owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* r.   -  work-in-progress of any type that is started by, in progress at the direction of, or owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* s.   -  software development in progress that is started by, in progress at the direction of, or owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;
* t.   -  app development in progress that is started by, in progress at the direction of, or owned or controlled by aixeno inc.;

Furthermore, in addition to the list detailed above, the company may respond to any threats received by immediately terminating, canceling, voiding, revoking, recalling, withdrawing, rescinding, repudiating, nullifying, disclaiming, denying, and/or making any other form or notice of cancellation as it may apply to any other completion of, delivery of, provision of, or access to: any activity, company information, company assets, use of company technology or company property; however those goods, services or any other things, may relate to the person or entity making any threats against the company.  
  
The company has the right to act at its own discretion anytime and it may communicate with law enforcement authorities anywhere in the world to provide evidence and formally file reports of threats, and it may at any time or place file legal claims of harm in any court of law anywhere in the world against the person(s), entity or entities, making threats against the company. Please see Washington State Law - RCW 9A.46.020.

The company aixeno inc. has the right to refuse service to any person(s) or entities for a variety of lawful reasons, and it will lawfully refuse to "do any business with" any person or entity that has made any threats against the company at any time.

#### 38\. Definitions Of Legal Terms, Words, And Phrases

**2-Step Verification, 2FA, 2.F.A. - Two-Factor Authentication** - electronic verification(s) of an end-user, consumer, or customer, at sign-in/log-in to an electronic resource, through a two-step process of evaluating an end-user's credentials by referring to and matching identical added secret codes and unique identifying information. The first step of sign-in is usually an end-user entering a username and password on a login webpage. The second step to continue a secure sign-in to get into a protected electronic resource is to require passage through a 2FA management system, which requires the end-user to use another separate digital device (other than the digital device used to sign-in to a resource) to generate and/or receive a random code of letters and numbers that is then entered by the end-user into the log-in page and evaluated for matching by the 2FA system protecting entry to the electronic resources. The purpose of using 2FA is to add another layer of security and identity verification of end-users attempting to sign-in to a computer system, before granting secure access to any protected electronic resources, so that if any usernames and passwords were to be stolen, fraudulent access would not be granted because the criminal would not have the added 2FA credentials to be verified as a lawful and verified end-user. An "electronic resource" may include: any computer system, computer networks, apps, software programs, protected webpages, messaging apps, financial services, banking webpages, or databases.

**Abandoned Property, Abandoned Property Law (USA State Law)** - money or intangible property held for a period of time with no owner contact: several U.S. States have differing laws applying to unclaimed property. Washington State Law regarding unclaimed property is available at this weblink:  [Washington Department of Revenue - Unclaimed Property](https://dor.wa.gov/education/industry-guides/restaurants-and-retailers-prepared-food/unclaimed-property#:~:text=When%20reported%20to%20the%20Department,a%20set%20period%20of%20time. "Unclaimed Property").

Acceptable use of any technology and/or any technology related service means that any user or users will not interfere directly or indirectly with any other consumers, customers, or end-users that are using the technology at any time. Acceptable use means that all of the company's digital solutions, digital technologies, products, and services will not suffer any hinderance, delay, deletion, disruption, destruction, or other any other type of harm, from any use of its technologies, solutions, and services, which may be caused by any consumer's, customer's, and end-user's unacceptable use or (unlawful use) at any time. **ai - a.i. - A.I. - artificial intelligence** - the use by humans (or other computers) of any computer technology, (hardware, software, network, combined technological systems, robots) used to process information and electronic data in an automatic, autonomous, and programmed manner that is step-wise or driven by a programmed algorithm, to perform any activity that is often or otherwise a human activity, such as analyzing data for pattern recognition and automatic/structured decision-making, generating a language based response, analysis of data, machine learning from existing data, answering data related questions from humans, using automated algorithmic search patterns from data, machine learning from any collection of data or datasets, performing calculations, rearranging data into new patterns for high-speed data processing, imagery analysis, generation of chat communications through a robots or bots for interactions or messaging of any kind, generate text and/or video, perform data search activities, answer questions, or for any other computer-based information processing, including using large language models to assist humans in solving complex problems through data and computer resources. AI is defined in the US Presidential [Executive Order on the Safe, Secure, and Trustworthy Development and Use of Artificial Intelligence](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/presidential-actions/2023/10/30/executive-order-on-the-safe-secure-and-trustworthy-development-and-use-of-artificial-intelligence/ "Executive Order on the Safe, Secure, and Trustworthy Development and Use of Artificial Intelligence")  _“artificial intelligence” or “AI” has the meaning set forth in 15 U.S.C. 9401(3): a machine-based system that can, for a given set of human-defined objectives, make predictions, recommendations, or decisions influencing real or virtual environments. Artificial intelligence systems use machine- and human-based inputs to perceive real and virtual environments; abstract such perceptions into models through analysis in an automated manner; and use model inference to formulate options for information or action." (Executive Order, Sec. 3. Definitions (b))._  Humans use artificial intelligence technologies by typing text into, or speaking conversationally with, an ai language model on a computer network server. **Assumption of Risk** - a person or entity choosing to accept the responsibility for the harms of loss, injury, damage, or disruption.

**Attribution of Ownership** - a person's right to be named as the author of intellectual property that is protected by copyright.

**Authority** - the legal right(s), legal permission(s), or source of legally defined boundaries, that altogether functions as an explicit legal basis to justify as lawful and reasonable any person's or entity's performance of a lawful action for themselves or acting for the benefit of another person or entity as an authorized agent. Authority is also the citation of or referral to a specific and detailed law, statute, code, contract term, license term, caselaw, court ruling, court decision, court order, legislative document, or other legal ruling, directive, order, or decree, of a government, as in an executive order of a Governor of a U.S. State or an executive order of the President of the United States. Authority may also be a legal order to not perform an action, as in a person or entity being prevented from acting by a legally valid court-ordered injunction or restraining order.

**Authorization** - official permission to do something: the process of requesting an express and official approval from and official permission from a legally authorized person. Authorization may also refer to a lawful document that grants official permission to do something. (See also “without authorization” accessing a protected computer, see the Computer Fraud and Abuse Act (“CFAA”), at 18 U.S.C. §§ 1030(a)(1), (a)(2), (a)(3), (a)(4), and (a)(5)(B)-(C).).

**Authorization of Payment(s) and Pre-Authorization of Payment(s)** -

**Authorized Access** - getting into and using a technology with permission and approval from a legally authorized person. (See also, the definitions of: "access," and "scope of access," and "unauthorized access" and "exceeding authorized access," and "unpaid access" and "fraudulent access").

**Authorization Pending** -

**Authorized** - any action that is done under an existing and legally valid approval or permission from a legally authorized person.

**Auto Pay, Automatic Payment** - payment that is automatic and electronic, according to prior consent of consumer, where money is authorized to be paid out of a consumer's bank account or credit card account to a business, in exchange for goods and services.

**Automatic Renewal** - with a consumer's prior consent, any voluntary reestablishment of a legal relationship created by a previously agreed upon but recently expired contract for a service.

**Average Use** - any quantity of something used by a consumer, customer, or end-user, such as a service quantity, as measured during a specific time-period that is calculated as an average during the same specific time-period.

**Bank Card** - any payment card issued by a bank or financial institution that is similar to a bank (credit union), to include without limitation: a debit card, where money is paid in before a transaction can be considered as paid in full, or a credit card, involving a loan of money to the consumer to complete a payment transaction.

**Bankruptcy** - the quality, state, condition, or posture of being insolvent: not having enough assets and money to pay debts and liabilities that are valid and are an obligation owed and to be repaid. The U.S. Bankruptcy Code is found in Title 11 of the U.S. Code.

**Barter** - exchanging goods and services of value through a trade without paying any money, as in "a like-kind exchange" of things of the same value.

**Beneficiary, Third-Party Beneficiary** - a person or entity that receives a benefit of property, money, or something of value, from a contract, insurance policy, wills, estates, trusts, or other gifts. A third-party beneficiary is a person or entity that receives a benefit from a contract made between two other parties.

**Benefit of the Bargain** - a legal principle that requires any party who breaches a contract to pay the other party suffering damages from the breach, to place the damaged party into an economic/financial position that is as good as what they would have received from the full performance of the contract as if the breach had not happened.

**Beta Test** - a second and last test of any new products, technologies, or services, created by a person, entity, or company, before releasing it to public consumer markets for sale and use by customers, consumers, and end-users.

**Bill Date** - the ending date of a billing period.

**Bill to Pay** - any bill created by a person, entity, or company, which is presented, delivered, communicated, or electronically sent to a consumer, customer, or end-user, for payment.

**Bill, Billed, Billing, Invoice, Invoicing** - a written (physical or electronic) detailed list of items, services, goods, products or other things, detailed by quantity and description and cost or price, that is delivered by a provider or seller to a buyer/consumer with the seller’s expectation that a buyer/consumer will pay for those things delivered to the consumer or made available for the consumer to use. The phrase "made available" includes electronic access to allow a consumer to use the electronic features, functions, information, data and other interactive elements of any digital solution and digital technology that is provided to consumers by this company.

**Billing Cycle** - the time-period interval between the days or dates of regular, periodic, and recurring bills and statement(s) of the account(s) for all consumers, customers, and/or end-users, describing, explaining, and calculating costs, prices, fees, taxes, and all other monetary amounts that are payable to the company for any transactions and for the provision of and delivery of goods and services.

**Billing Period** - the amount of time since the last bill date.

**Billing Policy** - a business contract formed by mutual agreement between a company and its consumers, end-users, and customers, defining and explaining all terms and conditions of how and when the exchange of goods and services will be accounted for and paid for through the transactions and activities of creating a detailed factual bill presented by the company to its consumers, end-users, and customers requesting money payment(s) for goods and services delivered, provided, and exchanged.

**Bi-Monthly** - every other month (a two-month time-period).

**Binding** - having the legal force of a valid obligation, valid liability, and/or valid legal duty, which must be performed according to terms and conditions of any agreement to be bound (as in a binding contract).

**Bi-Weekly** - every other week (a two-week time-period).

**BNPL, B.N.P.L.** - "buy now pay later" is a transaction where a customer buys something and pays for it with money from a loan provided by a seller, bank, credit union, bank card issuer, debit card issuer, credit card issuer, or any other financial institution: the customer's loan agreement requires making more than one (1) payment ( plus interest and fees ) over time to pay the full price of purchasing goods or services (plus paying the additional amounts of loan interest and fees). The "buy now pay later" transaction and loan results in a customer paying more money for something compared to paying the full price in cash at the original time of the sale.

**Breach, Breach of Contract, or Material Breach** - the failure to perform fully a contractual duty when it is due is a breach of contract. In the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements of this company, one example of a breach includes (without limitation); default, non-payment of billed invoice for digital solutions and digital technologies delivered to consumers. A “material breach” is a breach that is serious enough to justify the other party in abandoning the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements. A “material breach” is one that substantially defeats the purpose of the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements, or relates to an essential element of the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements, and deprives the injured party of a benefit that he or she or they would have reasonably expected to occur.

**Break Apart** - the action of taking something that is joined together and through legal actions then separating it into smaller parts or distinctly individual parts, as in breaking apart a partnership, or severing a joint venture into individual entities, or taking a service contract made of multiple combined services and breaking it apart into individual services.

**Browser, Web Browser** - a software application running on a digital device which is used to display electronic information from the internet, world-wide-web, or other web server(s).

**Bundle** - a combination of different goods and/or services into one inter-related and simultaneous: delivery of goods, service, transaction, product, advertisement, or offer of something of value.

**Business Expectancy** - future opportunities and profits that are a reasonable expectation of a party based upon some verifiable facts or reliable information; a relationship between parties contemplating a contract, with at least a reasonable expectation of fruition.” 80 Wn.2d at 84–85.

**Check** - a paper check is a draft drawn upon a bank, credit union, or other similar financial institution, for unconditional payment. Checks in the United States are legally categorized as "Negotiable Instruments" and the laws applying to checks are covered by Uniform Commercial Code Article 3. A negotiable instrument is a signed document that promises a payment to a specified person or assignee. Negotiable instruments are transferable, which allows the recipient to take the funds as cash. An eCheck is an electronic transfer of funds as the result of converting and negotiating a printed and signed paper check into an electronic transaction causing an electronic transfer of funds.

**Choice of Governing Law** - the choice of which jurisdiction’s law will apply to any contracts, terms of use agreements, license agreements, or other legal issues in a dispute.

**Class** - a group of persons, services, or goods, which have some facts, characteristics, elements, legal status, or activities, in common.

**Commercial Reasonableness, Commercially Reasonable** - a “Commercially Reasonable Effort” is a good faith effort made or attempted by a party to fulfill its contractual promises, obligations and legal duties as already defined in a written contract where that party’s level of “effort” is: (a) an effort that any reasonable business entity in similar circumstances would have accomplished, applied or used in a similar situation; (b) a level of action and/or effort that is economically and financially prudent; (c) an effort that is considered standard, customary and typical in the specific industry for the specific type of transactions or actions performed under the specific type of contract; (d) an effort that fairly and efficiently balances any competing interests or tradeoffs faced by the parties to a contract involving any of their resources, skills, costs, capacity and available time, geographic places of performance under the contract, available methods and manner of performing under the contract; (e) an appropriate level of effort that fairly balances any party’s financial resources, financial profitability versus avoiding a financial loss beyond or less than any financial breakeven point for any level of performance or action under the contract; (f) a level of effort that is reasonably expected to be well within a party’s business expertise and business practices in the normal course of its business. “Commercially Reasonable Efforts” does not mean and does not require: (1) that a party must guarantee a fail-safe outcome of success or profit to be achieved at all costs no matter how extreme the effort or expenditure may seem to a reasonable person under similar circumstances; (2) an effort that attempts to spend monetary resources wastefully, or requires efforts that commit economic waste, by pursuing every conceivable effort or action no matter how extreme it may seem to a reasonable person under similar circumstances; (3) a level of effort that is demanded by another party that has not already been presented in writing and agreed to in writing by all parties to the contract before the demand is made; (4) a level of effort that requires any party to destroy, damage, and/or sacrifice its own economic and business interests by suffering an impossible situation of becoming liable for or experiencing unanticipated and substantial financial losses to perform its contractual obligations; (5) a level of effort that results in any party spending money to pay for expenses that exceed, or incurring liabilities that exceed, any dollar amount that is not expressly stated in the valid contract prior to the contract being performed; (6) an effort that would likely subject a party to perform its contractual obligations through any conduct that would be materially (significantly) adverse to its existence as a ‘going concern’ or endanger its regulatory requirements to establish and maintain any net capital requirements and/or solvency requirements; (7) an effort that would likely harm any party’s “business expectancy” that it may by its efforts reasonably expect (at a minimum) to break-even financially by performing its contractual obligations and expect to receive the benefits of the bargain(s) contemplated by the contract; (8) an effort that requires a party to take any action that would cause it to incur expenses or suffer a financial harm or detriment that is not reasonable in proportion to the benefits under the business contract; (9) a level of effort that would imperil any party’s reasonable and lawful business strategies or economic interests or require it to disregard those interests to its own peril; (10) an effort that would require any action that would subject a party to increase its liabilities on a voluntary or involuntary basis; (11) a level of effort or expense that would require any party to violate any covenants or conditions with its own creditors, lenders, banks, shareholders, bondholders, insurers or governmental authorities; (12) any effort that would expose any party to any illegal actions or put a party in legal jeopardy or a level of effort that violates public policy; (13) any level of effort that would expose any party to any violation of any regulations or laws imposed upon it by the nature of any party’s holding any license, permit, authorization or other regulatory approval to conduct its business, or interfere with a party’s good-faith compliance with those regulatory requirements, from Federal, State, Local or Self-Regulatory Organizations; (14) any level of effort that will likely cause any party to breach the then existing contract (voluntarily or involuntarily).

**Commercial Software** - any app and/or software program that is published, distributed, and sold for a profit.

**Commercial Tort Claim** - UCC § 9-102 (a)(13) any legal claim based on tort laws where the claimant is an organization; or the claimant is an individual and the claim is from activities of the claimant’s business or profession and does not include requests for money damages based upon personal injury to, or the death of, an individual.

**Commercial Use, Commercial Usage, Without a Valid Technology License** - use of a tool, thing, or technology anywhere, including use through or in a marketplace of commerce, a business, or other entity, where the use of technology is attempted, made, completed, or exchanged in any transaction, where at least one of the parties to the use has an intention and goal charging money or something of value in exchange for the use of technology in order to, or primarily to, make a profit, and where at least on party to the technology use, does not possess a lawful and valid license to use the technology that is part of a commercial use. Any person, business, or other entity has the capacity to use any technology for commercial uses. A commercial use of technology without a valid technology license also involves the use of technology or use of any elements of the technology, that are involved in any way in another sale, bargain, conveyance, transaction, exchange of information, movement of technology, or commercial use of the technology that involves the exchange of money with a third-party, where the third-party does not have a valid technology license.

**Commercial Use, Commercial Usage** - use of a tool, thing, or technology anywhere, including use through or in a marketplace of commerce, a business, or other entity, where the use of technology is attempted, made, completed, or exchanged in any transaction, where at least one of the parties to the use has an intention and goal charging money or something of value in exchange for the use of technology in order to, or primarily to, make a profit. Commercial use also occurs in any business-related bargain, sale, barter, exchange, or any other conveyance of property or use of anything of value for a business purpose. Any person, business, or other entity has the capacity to use any technology for commercial uses. A commercial use of technology also involves the use of technology or the use of any elements of the technology, which are involved in any way in another sale, bargain, conveyance, transaction, exchange of information, movement of technology, or commercial use of the technology that involves the exchange of money with a third-party.

**Company Property** - any type of property, assets, rights, title, interests, rents, profits, income, financial gains, and any other thing(s) of value that can be owned, possessed, used, and enjoyed for lawful business use, which is either partially or entirely owned and/or controlled by the corporation aixeno inc.

**Contract** - a written agreement between two or more parties, including promises, terms, conditions, created when an offer is accepted, consideration is defined, and performance is agreed to by the parties. Washington State Law defines a contract as a legally enforceable promise or set of promises. \[In order for a promise or set of promises to be legally enforceable, there must be mutual assent and consideration. “A contract is a promise or set of promises for the breach of which the law gives a remedy, or the performance of which the law recognizes as a duty.” An agreement, on the other hand, “is a manifestation of mutual assent by two or more persons to one another,” and “has a wider meaning than contract, bargain or promise.” Corbit v. J. I. Case Co., 70 Wn.2d 522, 531, 424 P.2d 290 (1967), quoting Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 3 and comment (a).

(i.e., a wholesale cost for something of value may be five dollars, but the final selling price to an end user may be six dollars plus taxes and fees).

**Cost Limit** - a number representing a maximum quantity of grand total costs that must not be exceeded.

**Cyber Incident** - a cyber incident is the same as “incident” under 44 U.S.C. 3552(b)(2)

**Cyber, Cybersecurity** - electronic information systems, software, systems, the internet, and other computer networks are often referred to collectively as "cyber." Cybersecurity is a systematic evaluation, protection, and defense of information technology systems, networks, computers, programs to reduce or eliminate harmful loss of data from digital attacks, unauthorized intrusions, fraudulent use of data, theft of data, or other damage or harm, and any effort or expense to upgrade, maintain, or remediate cyber protections for any information technology systems, networks, computers, programs.

**Cyberattack** - Any kind of malicious and illegal activity against computer systems that attempts to collect, disrupt, deny, degrade, or destroy information system resources or the information (data) itself. Please also see a cyber “incident” under 44 U.S.C. 3552(b)(2)

**Cyberstalking** - illegal use of electronic communication to threaten, harass, or otherwise act with an intent to cause another person to experience a fear of death, serious bodily harm, or intentionally inflicted emotional distress. In the USA, there are Federal and State Laws against cyberstalking, making it a crime punishable by fines and/or imprisonment.

**D2C, D.2.C., DTC - Direct to Consumer** - retail services or goods are sold and/or delivered directly from the company to a retail consumer without a middle person or entity (no wholesale distribution channel as a middle processing step).

**Damages** - an amount of money claimed to be owing or sued for in a legal action made by a person or party for alleged injury or loss to a person or property, where the amount of money damages, if awarded by a court of law, would serve as compensation for an injury or loss. Actual damages are those losses that were reasonably foreseeable, at the time the contract was made, as a probable result of a breach. A loss may be foreseeable as a probable result of a breach because it follows from the breach either (a) in the ordinary course of events, or (b) as a result of special circumstances, beyond the ordinary course of events, that the party in breach had reason to know.

**Data Breach** - means a breach of cybersecurity resulting in the accidental, unintended, or unlawful destruction, loss, alteration, unauthorized disclosure of, or access to, electronic computer data that is created, updated, transmitted, stored or otherwise processed by, in, or through any computer, computer system, computer network, software, apps, databases, or other digital device.

**Data Leak** - the unlawful and unauthorized disclosure of, or acquisition of, personally identifiable information of customers, clients, end-users, or consumers, which if disclosed without prior consent will most likely harm a person or entity in terms of their safety, financial security, personal security, confidentiality, reputation, or integrity of personal information, to include without limitation: an individual’s first name (or initial) and last name, U.S. Social Security Number, Driver’s license number, state-issued ID card number, account number, credit or debit card numbers, username, security code, access code, PIN, or passwords, medical history, health information, biometric information, email address, Tax ID number, or any other personally identifiable information that is confidential and legally protected.

**Data Limit** - a maximum amount of electronic data that cannot be exceeded in any action or use by an end-user, consumer, customer, or client, involving electronic data, to include without limitation: storage, transfer, downloading, uploading, processing, copying, pasting, storage, creation, saving, access, reading, writing, updating, editing, printing, retrieval, calculations, processing cycles, computing, sharing, or any other thing that involves electronic data of any kind, located anywhere at any time, and under the ownership, management, creation, control, use, or custody and protection of aixeno inc.

**Data Scraping** - electronic viewing, copying, and data collection from public websites without prior permission, gathering in an automated manner any available text, images, videos, and other website information by using software, apps, and/or a.p.i. methods. Scraping the contents of websites may be illegal in some jurisdictions that prohibit unauthorized access and use of information that is legally protected, copyrighted, personally identifiable, legally privileged against disclosure, or sealed under a court-order.

**Data** - information (physical or electronic), facts, statistics, details, evidence, material, figures, numbers, characters and/or any other images or symbols represented electronically or physically, signals, any bits or bytes of information (digital or analog) that may be processed electronically or mechanically, financial information, scientific information, legal information, observational information, monetary information, stock price information, market data information, accounting information, any information that can be used in mathematical operations and/or functions, knowledge, testimony, any information that can be communicated, any information that can be recorded into any medium (tangible or intangible), anything that can be analyzed to discover a pattern and lead to a conclusion, description or explanation.

**DBN - D.B.N. - Data Breach Notice** - a formal notice and document (electronic and/or paper format) describing and explaining any breach of cybersecurity resulting in the accidental, unintended, or unlawful destruction, loss, alteration, unauthorized disclosure of, or access to, electronic computer data that is created, updated, transmitted, stored or otherwise processed by, in, or through any computer, computer system, computer network, software, apps, databases, or other digital device. Several jurisdictions require specific notice formats and deadlines for any data breach notifications. Please see some examples at the following weblinks:  [Data Breach Notice - Washington State](https://www.atg.wa.gov/data-breach-notifications "Data Breach Notice - Washington State")  and  [Text of Law applying to Data Breach Notice and Frequently Asked Questions - Washington State](https://www.atg.wa.gov/HB1071-FAQ "Data Breach Notice - Text of Washington State Law and Frequently Asked Questions").

**DDOS - D.D.O.S.** - a distributed denial-of-service (DDoS) attack is a malicious attempt overwhelm and block an electronic resource with excessive access requests to achieve an illegal goal of disrupting any normal internet traffic getting through to a website, webpage, portal, transaction, webapp, or other internet and/or website related resource, so that it cannot be used in any way. Please see the weblink:  [DDOS description at Cloudflare.com](https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ddos/what-is-a-ddos-attack/ "DDOS description at Cloudflare.com").

**Deadline** - a calendar date and time that quantifies an absolute limit of when something must be completed, done, finished, delivered, submitted, turned-in, turned over, handed over, sold, performed, stopped, perfected, filed, transferred, transacted, recorded, paid, calculated, generated, manufactured, assembled, tested, presented, communicated, displayed, published, processed, created in final form, offered, purchased, and altogether put into a finished and final form, format or state of being, for a specific use.

**Debit Card** - a card issued by a bank, credit union, or other financial institution, which is electronically connected to a specific account allowing for authorized money to be paid out of an account, decreasing the balance amount remaining and available in the account after a payment has been made.

**Debit** - a money transaction where money is paid out of an account, decreasing the balance amount remaining and available in the account after a payment has been made.

**Deception, Online Deception** - use of information in emails, messages, or on the internet and world-wide-web, which is information that is false, fraudulent, untruthful, and used in the commission of a crime by misleading, misinforming, and/or making another person or entity believe, do, or communicate something that is not true. Deceptive information is often used when committing an online crime during attempts to illegally get some personal advantage, gain, money, or profit, through fraud.

**Decompile** - convert computer codes and instructions existing in apps and/or software already in its final compiled and executable form, into readable human language and logical instructions. (Decompile is the opposite of "compile.")

**Deep Fake - Deep-Fake** - a digital creation of images, videos, speech, and other electronic information, which is an unauthorized and unlawful misrepresentation of a person's image, likeness, speech, actions, or other fraudulent characteristics that did not actually occur in the real world. In some jurisdictions, deep-fake imagery, video, speech, are illegal.

**Deep-Fake Image** - a digital creation of images, videos, speech, and other electronic information, which is an unauthorized and unlawful misrepresentation of a person's image, likeness, speech, actions, or other fraudulent characteristics that did not actually occur in the real world. In some jurisdictions, deep-fake imagery, video, speech, are illegal.

**Deep-Fake Video** - a digital creation of images, videos, speech, and other electronic information, which is an unauthorized and unlawful misrepresentation of a person's image, likeness, speech, actions, or other fraudulent characteristics that did not actually occur in the real world. In some jurisdictions, deep-fake imagery, video, speech, are illegal.

**Defamation** - false statements made with malice that tend to expose a living person to (a) hatred, contempt, ridicule, or obloquy, or to deprive him or her of the benefit of public confidence or social intercourse, or to injure him or her in his or her business or occupation, or (b) to injure any person, corporation, or association in his, her, or its business or occupation. Please see Washington Law "RCW 7.96 - Uniform Correction Or Clarification Of Defamation Act."

**Default** - failure of a party to a contract, agreement, terms of use agreement, license agreement, to fail to do something that is legally binding and required of them that should have been done in a specific time, place, manner, and payment or performance of something, according to the terms of the contract and/or agreement.

**Delay** - the time period when something with a pre-existing deadline date and time has been postponed, slowed, or barely moved forward at a pace acceptable to a completion time schedule defined in an agreement, contract, or as suggested by industry custom, or as required by a court-order or a regulatory filing deadline.

**Delegation** - the act of granting written authority or entrusting to another person or party a legal right to act as an agent or representative of a principal person or principal party.

**Deliberate** - a choice or decision that is made after a careful, conscientious, thorough, intentional, voluntary, and diligent consideration of facts and consequences of human actions, evidence, circumstances, options, alternatives, transactions, burdens, and goals.

**Deliberation** - the mental process and state of mind of carefully considering issues and options before making a decision or taking an action.

**Delivery Date** - an exact and definite calendar date and time when the formal action of voluntarily transferring something from one person or place to another or place, actually occurs.

**Device, Digital Device** - a computer chip driven electronic device, network, or system, which processes electronic data through the generation and use of any digital timing signals operating at greater than 9,000 cycles per second (9 kHz). A digital device is used to create, store, update, transmit, process, and otherwise function as an information processing device in the human use of electronic information, data, imagery, communications, and transactions, of normal everyday life. Many different types of electronic equipment and consumer products are digital devices because they contain circuitry using electronic digital timing signals. Examples of digital devices include computers, cable tv, calculators, digital watches and clocks, automotive electronic systems, GPS navigation devices, televisions, video game handheld devices, telephones, smartphones, microwave ovens, video cassette recorders, security alarm systems, printers, fax machines, copy machines, smartwatches, medical monitoring equipment, network computer servers, navigation systems in airplanes, and several other computerized equipment that people encounter in their daily lives.

**Digital Services Act, DSA (European Union)** - The DSA regulates online intermediaries and platforms such as marketplaces, social networks, content-sharing platforms, app stores, and online travel and accommodation platforms. Its main goal is to prevent illegal and harmful activities online and the spread of disinformation. It ensures user safety, protects fundamental rights, and creates a fair and open online platform environment.  [https://commission.europa.eu/strategy-and-policy/priorities-2019-2024/europe-fit-digital-age/digital-services-act\_en](https://commission.europa.eu/strategy-and-policy/priorities-2019-2024/europe-fit-digital-age/digital-services-act_en "Digital Services Act, DSA (European Union) - https://commission.europa.eu/strategy-and-policy/priorities-2019-2024/europe-fit-digital-age/digital-services-act_en")

**Distribution of Software or Code** - delivering, publishing, apportioning, giving out, transmitting, transferring, software code and/or app code.

**DMCA - D.M.C.A. - Digital Millennium Copyright Act** - In 1998, Congress passed the Digital Millennium Copyright Act (DMCA), which amended U.S. copyright law to address important parts of the relationship between copyright and the internet. The three main updates were (1) establishing protections for online service providers in certain situations if their users engage in copyright infringement, including by creating the notice-and-takedown system, which allows copyright owners to inform online service providers about infringing material so it can be taken down; (2) encouraging copyright owners to give greater access to their works in digital formats by providing them with legal protections against unauthorized access to their works (for example, hacking passwords or circumventing encryption); and (3) making it unlawful to provide false copyright management information (for example, names of authors and copyright owners, titles of works) or to remove or alter that type of information in certain circumstances. [https://www.copyright.gov/dmca](https://www.copyright.gov/dmca/ "DMCA - https://www.copyright.gov/dmca").

**DNS - D.N.S.** - "Domain Name System" which is a lookup database used on the internet and world wide web to lookup domain names and its assigned IP address, making it possible for end-users to use web browsers to navigate the internet and find specific web pages.

**Donate, Donation** - the act of giving a gift of something in order to help a charity, a person, or another organization, often given for free without compensation, payment, or other legal forms of consideration.

**Downgrade** - the choice and action of moving from one "version" of a digital solution or digital technology, down to a different digital solution or digital technology, which has fewer features, functions, capacities, storage space, transaction limits, time limits, other technology limits, or to move from a paid subscription down to a free and more basic subscription of a digital solution or digital technology. Downgrade is the opposite of upgrade. Please also see the definitions of "version," "upgrade."

**Download (data or information)** - the action of transferring data, images, or other digital information down to an end-user's computer or digital device, "downstream" from a larger computer server on an intranet or downstream from a computer server on the internet or world wide web.

**Downtime** - the total duration of time when any computer resource, network connection, internet connection, connection to the world wide web, webpage, or any other digital resource, is "not working" and is offline, unusable, or completely blocked from being used as intended or as it is usually functioning for an intended purpose and use.

**Doxing - Doxxing - D0xing** - doxing, doxxing, or d0xing, is the unauthorized disclosure and publishing on public platforms the personally identifiable information about a human person, or persons that are members of any entity or organization: it is usually posted on and published over the internet, a news site, a website, or a social media platform. Doxxing is a violation of U.S. Federal Laws: (1) The Interstate Communications Statute, and (2) The Interstate Stalking Statute, in addition to U.S. State Laws.

**Due And Payable** - any valid debt owed to another that is subject to immediate collection and payment in full because a lawful due date has been reached or passed, or some other term and condition of the debt agreement has been fulfilled.

**Due Date** - the deadline day on the calendar that is the very last day when a payment is due and payable to be considered "paid according to terms and conditions of a service subscription, a service payment, or any other type of sale and purchase terms and conditions for digital goods or digital services from this company." Due Date applies to "new charges" that are due and payable.

**Due Upon Receipt - Payment Due Upon Receipt** - payment to the company is due immediately upon receipt (when bill is received) by a consumer, customer, or end user, for an amount of money that is billed for goods and services as described in a contract, bill of sale, subscription, service agreement, or another legal document.

**Duet AI (Google)** - please see this weblink:  [Google Duet AI](https://cloud.google.com/ai/duet-ai "Google Duet AI").

**Duplicate Transaction(s)** - any additional transaction that is an exact copy or exact copies of an original transaction, when only one (1) transaction was intended, requested, and authorized.

**Duration of Use** - the total duration of time when something is actively used. Also, the "lifetime of the license" defined in a license agreement: a limited timeline of when the license agreement begins and ends (e.g., (1). a 'monthly recurring subscription license' would be good and valid for one calendar month, (2). an 'annual license' would be in existence and valid for one year (365 days), while (3). a 'perpetual license' would be valid forever). It is also a factual statement that quantifies how long something was used.

**E2EE - E.2.E.E.** - End to End Encryption.

**ECC - Elliptic Curve Cryptography** - please see this weblink:  [ECC - Elliptic Curve Cryptography](https://blog.cloudflare.com/a-relatively-easy-to-understand-primer-on-elliptic-curve-cryptography "ECC - Elliptic Curve Cryptography").

**Edition (version)** - any published media, app, software program, web application, or any other thing that is published, and is identified by a discrete and unique number, specific to the point in time when it was published during the product's life cycle.

**Effective Date** - the date, and/or data and time, when something happens or begins to happen: a date in time that some legal act or acts or contracts, agreements, licenses, or transactions, will come into effect, will become existing as "operable and in-force," and becomes legally enforceable.

**Electronic Access** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are exclusive and protected against unauthorized entry into encrypted digital resources and requires that all users must pass through an initial challenge blocking step by using authorized sign-in credentials before being granted permission to use the digital resources that are encrypted and/or protected.

**Electronic Billing** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for sending bills to users for payment.

**Electronic Communication** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for communications between two (2) or more persons or computer machines.

**Electronic Data Processing** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for processing data of any type, including without limitation: text, messages, email, images, videos, media, or any data that is in digital form.

**Electronic Delivery** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for delivery to another person or entity, of any electronic digital data, apps, software, information, or any other digital resources.

**Electronic Notice** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for communicating any type of notice, information, message, or any type of financial or legal notifications.

**Electronic Payment** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for financial payment transactions.

**Electronic Resource** - any computer system, computer networks, apps, software programs, protected webpages, messaging apps, financial services, banking webpages, or databases.

**Electronic Signature** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for identifying and verifying a legally valid signature of an authorized person or entity.

**Electronic Transaction** - any electronic digital resources, computers, and systems that are used for authorized transactions.

**email - Email** - electronic mail.

**email address - Email Address** - electronic mail address of one specific user email account and its electronic message destination address for receiving and sending electronic mail.

A "consumer," means any person or entity that uses any solutions, services or products created or provided by aixeno inc. A "consumer" includes (without limitation), any persons, and entities commonly referred to as: businesses, non-profits, governments, non-government organizations, charitable organizations, educational institutions, and scientific organizations (and/or anyone using computer resources of any of those end-users).

**Enjoyment Of Use** - a legal right to own, occupy, possess, and lawfully use property.

**Enroll** - to register, transcribe, sign-up for something, or enter information into an official record.

**EON - E.O.N.** - edge of network

**Error** - mistake, something that is incorrect or inaccurate.

**Error Resolution** - actions, procedures, and company processes that use commercially reasonable efforts to remedy, resolve, or fix any mistake, involving something that is incorrect or inaccurate.

**Error Resolution Policy** - a company policy relating to the actions, procedures, and company processes that use commercially reasonable efforts to remedy, resolve, or fix any mistake, involving something that is incorrect or inaccurate.

**Estimated Cost** - a good faith forecast of total costs at a specific time in the future when something is finished, delivered, completed, or made available for use, based upon current market costs for goods and services, analysis, calculations, and probabilities.

**Estimated Use** - a good faith forecast of total quantifiable "use" of a digital resource by end-users, at a specific time in the future when something is able to be used, i.e., "the average data transferred per user each month is 1 Gig of data" based upon calculations of actual quantifiable use in the present, combined with analyses, calculations, and probabilities.

**ETL - E.T.L.** - Extract, Transform, Load data from several sources into one electronic database for further use, processing, reference, analysis, and other computer processing.

**EULA, End-User License Agreement, License Agreement** - the license agreement that the end-user consumer agrees to be bound by, while using any digital solutions and digital technologies of the company aixeno inc. and while using any technology through any of the company's websites. (The words "consumer," and "customer," and "end-user" are used as synonyms. A "consumer," means any person or entity that uses any solutions, services or products created or provided by aixeno inc. A "consumer" includes (without limitation), any persons, and entities commonly referred to as: businesses, non-profits, governments, non-government organizations, charitable organizations, educational institutions, and scientific organizations).

**Exceeding Authorized Access** - also described as: “exceeds authorized access,” sometimes also phrased “exceeding authorized access,” is the accessing a protected computer that goes beyond any scope of authorized access known by a person before the access occurred, please see the Computer Fraud and Abuse Act (“CFAA”) at 18 U.S.C. §§ 1030(a)(1), (a)(2), and (a)(4). (See also, the definitions of: "access," and "scope of access," and "authorized access" and "unauthorized access" and "unpaid access" and "fraudulent access.")

**Exchange, Exchanges, Rights of Exchange** - the act of transferring interests between parties, where the interest is given over to get something else of value: for consideration, for payment, and for anything else of value. Please see also: "like-kind exchange." Please also see "Return," and "Rights of Return," and "Trade-In," in these definitions.

**Exemption, Tax Exemption** - freedom from a duty, liability, or an exception to something that must be paid. A tax exemption is a quantifiable dollar amount that will not be subject to a tax being imposed or paid.

**Expectation of Privacy** - a belief that a person is exercising their constitutional and lawful rights to protect their private information from unlawful intrusion, unlawful disclosure, or to be free from any unlawful breaking of their Fourth Amendment Rights under the U.S. Constitution. U.S. States have laws protecting privacy, in addition to U.S. Federal Laws.

**Expectation** - a belief that something will happen based on a series of actions.

**Expected Cost** - a belief that a specific total cost is most likely, based upon projected and estimated costs from evidence, facts, circumstances, analyses, and probable outcomes.

**Expected Use** - use of something as it was designed, engineered, marketed, and most likely to be used in the real world by a majority of users.

**Fraud** - a knowingly reckless concealment of facts, or a knowing misrepresentation of facts known by the bad actor to be false, or an outright deliberate false representation, or an unconscionable transaction, made in order to induce another person to act or commit an act that results in their harm. See also the definition of: "wire fraud."

**Fraudulent Access** - a knowingly reckless concealment of facts, or a knowing misrepresentation of facts known by the bad actor to be false, or an outright deliberate false representation, or an unconscionable transaction, or a false promise, made in order to induce another person to act or commit an act that results in their harm by unlawful access to something, for example, a fraudulent access to an unlicensed technology that harms the victim of the fraud by subjecting them to legal jeopardy and criminal or civil penalties. (See also, the definitions of: "wire fraud," "access," and "scope of access," and "authorized access" and "unauthorized access" and "exceeding authorized access," and "unpaid access.")

**Fraudulent Conveyance** - a transfer of an interest in property for little or no consideration (or money) where the transfer is made for the purpose of hindering, delaying, or defeating a creditor by attempting to place the property out of the reach of the creditor.

**Fraudulent Use** - a knowingly reckless concealment of facts, or a knowing misrepresentation of facts known by the bad actor to be false, or an outright deliberate false representation, or an unconscionable transaction, or a false promise, made in order to induce another person to act or commit an act that results in their harm by unlawful use of something, for example, a fraudulent use of an unlicensed technology that harms the victim of the fraud by subjecting them to legal jeopardy and criminal or civil penalties. (See also, the definitions of: "wire fraud," "actual use," and "adverse use," and "fraudulent use," and "intended use," and "scope of use").

**Free License** - a general license agreement to use something that costs nothing. It also means a general license agreement that applies to any market of end-users, governing the use of digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, by many end-users and made available for free to any end-user.

**Free Trial** - a prospective buyer may "try using something for free" during a limited amount of time and within resources restrictions, before paying money to a seller to buy and own it exclusively.

**Free** - some goods or services available to use, have, own, take, transfer, or benefit from, without first paying any cost, price, fee, exchange of anything of value, or transfer and give up any amount of money or thing of value. It also means a general license agreement that applies to any market of end-users, governing the use of digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, by many end-users and made available for free to any end-user.

**Freeware** - proprietary code, apps, and software normally offered for sale, which is instead voluntarily given to the public for free. It is not the same as "free software" and it is not the same as "open-source free software."

**Frozen, Freeze** - services, transactions, goods, assets, contracts, money, business activities, or any other thing of value, is stopped, paused, blocked, delayed, locked, prevented from being used, immobilized, or in any other way held and prevented from being used, on a permanent or temporary basis.

**GST - G.S.T.** - a Canadian tax imposed upon Canadian persons, Canadian businesses, and other Canadian taxable entities. A goods and services tax (GST) is a tax that consumers and businesses pay on most goods and services sold or provided in Canada and also a tax imposed on cross-border digital products and services received or used by Canadian persons, businesses, and other taxable entities. In New Brunswick, Newfoundland and Labrador, Nova Scotia, Ontario and Prince Edward Island, the GST has been blended with the provincial sales tax and is called the harmonized sales tax (HST). A provincial sales tax (PST) or a retail sales tax (RST), may be added to the GST taxes in some provinces of Canada. A Québec Sales Tax (QST) is imposed in the Canadian Province of Québec.

Viewing the agreements as an entire integrated document, interpreting particular language in the context of other provisions in the agreement's documents, shows that the parties to intended to form binding terms and conditions for the provision and use of digital solutions and digital technologies. “Intent of Parties” specifies with certainty and expresses unambiguously the parties’ state of mind and goals, describing with sufficiently clear detail what they intended to provide and benefit from through the making of and performance of binding agreements and licenses.

**License & Revocable License** - permission granted to another person by the company to lawfully use something of value created by the company without passing ownership to another person. A "license," as in 'software license,' is a legal term, meaning that a license is a legally binding agreement between the company, aixeno inc., and an end-user, related to the lawful use of the digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, created by aixeno inc. A revocable license is any license that can or may be canceled, withdrawn, reversed, undone, or annulled.

**License Types** - the types of license agreements aixeno inc. offers are: Free License, Trial License, Paid License, Custom License. **Free License** - a general license agreement that applies to any market of end-users, governing the use of digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, by many end-users and made available for free to any end-user. **Trial License** - a general license agreement that applies to a specifically limited number of days of free use (e.g., 14 days) to allow a potential end-user to "try before you buy." This license agreement may be issued to any market of end-users, governing the use of digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, by many end-users and made available for free during a limited time to any public market. **Paid License** - a general license agreement that applies to any market of end-users, governing the use of digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, by many customers in a public market and made available for paid use - ( end-users pay money to the company aixeno inc., to use the licensed technology ). **Custom License** - a unique license agreement and/or service agreement that involves the creation of or requires any combination of: (a). custom-made digital electronic products, services, and data; (b). a unique combination of contract services, service level agreements, and existing technologies created by aixeno inc.; (c). long-term agreements governing digital electronic products, services, and data; (d). requests to create any type of brand-new technologies involving aixeno inc. digital electronic products, services, and data; (e). any other license agreement for any end-user that is not already defined by the "license types" already listed above.

**Linking To Sources (ai)** -

**Llama-2 LLM** -  [Meta AI - Llama](https://llama.meta.com/ "Meta AI - Llama").

**LLM - L.L.M. - Large Language Model** - human interaction with a computer using natural human language for questions and answers from an enormous data source. An LLM is often made from a software program, database, and a vast dataset of text information, which is evaluated by machine learning algorithms to examine and analyze language data through several artificial neural network matrices to discover statistical patterns of word frequencies, which could be used to form statistically plausible answers to questions given to the computer as prompts. A Large Language Model often requires reinforcement training from humans, significant computer processing and network resources, and several million dollars in total research and development costs to produce a functional LLM. The artificial intelligence of a Large Language Model is its software program code acting on language model data by relying on machine learning results to simulate human intelligence during the "chat-based" exchange of information. Examples of ai models and ai technologies, products, and services, may be found on this list:    [ai list - ai from other vendors](https://aixeno.com/ailist.html "ai list - ai from other vendors").

**Metered Use, Metered Usage** -

**MFA - M.F.A. - Multi-Factor Authentication** - electronic verification(s) of an end-user, consumer, or customer, at sign-in/log-in to an electronic resource, through two-step process (or multiple step processes) of evaluating an end-user's credentials by referring to and matching identical added secret codes and unique identifying information. The first step of sign-in is usually an end-user entering a username and password on a login webpage. The second and subsequent steps to continue a secure sign-in to get into a protected electronic resource is to require passage through a MFA management system, which requires the end-user to use another separate digital device (other than the digital device used to sign-in to a resource) to generate and/or receive a random codes of letters and numbers that is then entered by the end-user into the log-in page and evaluated for matching by the MFA system protecting entry to the electronic resources. The purpose of using MFA is to add another layer of security and identity verification of end-users attempting to sign-in to a computer system, before granting secure access to any protected electronic resources, so that if any usernames and passwords were to be stolen, fraudulent access would not be granted because the criminal would not have the added MFA credentials to be verified as a lawful and verified end-user. An "electronic resource" may include: any computer system, computer networks, apps, software programs, protected webpages, messaging apps, financial services, banking webpages, or databases. (Please also see the definition of 2FA).

**PST - P.S.T.** - a Canadian tax imposed upon Canadian persons, Canadian businesses, and other Canadian taxable entities. A goods and services tax (GST) is a tax that consumers and businesses pay on most goods and services sold or provided in Canada and also a tax imposed on cross-border digital products and services received or used by Canadian persons, businesses, and other taxable entities. In New Brunswick, Newfoundland and Labrador, Nova Scotia, Ontario and Prince Edward Island, the GST has been blended with the provincial sales tax and is called the harmonized sales tax (HST). A provincial sales tax (PST) or a retail sales tax (RST), may be added to the GST taxes in some provinces of Canada. A Québec Sales Tax (QST) is imposed in the Canadian Province of Québec.

**QCS (Quantum Computing Software)** - computer software used by a quantum computer: software that uses logical circuits and algorithms based upon the scientific principles of quantum theory, quantum mechanics, quantum electrodynamics, quantum chromodynamics.

**QST - Q.S.T.** - a Canadian tax imposed upon Canadian persons, Canadian businesses, and other Canadian taxable entities. A goods and services tax (GST) is a tax that consumers and businesses pay on most goods and services sold or provided in Canada and also a tax imposed on cross-border digital products and services received or used by Canadian persons, businesses, and other taxable entities. In New Brunswick, Newfoundland and Labrador, Nova Scotia, Ontario and Prince Edward Island, the GST has been blended with the provincial sales tax and is called the harmonized sales tax (HST). A provincial sales tax (PST) or a retail sales tax (RST), may be added to the GST taxes in some provinces of Canada. A Québec Sales Tax (QST) is imposed in the Canadian Province of Québec.

**Quantity** - in technology, it means a numerical description of an amount of something that can be quantified, measured, and counted: magnitude, size, volume, transactions, subscriptions, payments, computing operations per second. In billing and payment, it is the quantity and number of things provided, accessed, used, consumed, exchanged, transferred, or otherwise delivered to a consumer, customer, end-user: it is a thing counted to use in a multiplication of price times the number of things exchanged in a transaction, or things counted to use in a multiplication of cost times quantity to give a resulting subtotal amount of money to pay.

**Quarterly** - a three (3) month time period. During a calendar year, the quarter ends every three months at the end of March, June, September, and December.

**Ransom, Ransomware** - Ransomware is a form of malicious software or app designed to unlawfully encrypt files on a digital device making any files locked and the systems that rely on them unusable. Criminals then demand ransom in exchange for unlocking and decryption. Please also see:  [https://www.stopransomware.gov](https://www.stopransomware.gov/ "US Government - Stop Ransomware  -  https://www.stopransomware.gov")

**RCW or R.C.W.** - the Revised Code of Washington ("RCW") is the compilation of all permanent laws now in force. It is a collection of Session Laws (enacted by the Legislature, and signed by the Governor, or enacted via the initiative process), arranged by topic, with amendments added and repealed laws removed. It does not include temporary laws such as appropriations acts. The official version of the RCW is published by the Statute Law Committee and the Code Reviser. https://apps.leg.wa.gov/rcw/

**Threat, Threats Against the Company** - a communicated intent to inflict harm or loss on another or onto another's property. A threat against the company is considered to be any threat of any kind, from anywhere in the world, which is a communication in any form or format (verbal, written, electronic, digital, analog or otherwise) made against the company (directly or indirectly) by any consumer, end-user, any bot, robot, chatbot, or any human person or other entity that is intended in any way to negatively affect the company by: using words threatening violence and/or destruction, inciting others to commit crimes or violence or destruction, causing harm of any kind, withhold something of value, interfere with or disrupt anything related to the company's normal course of business, cause any risk of financial loss, cause legal jeopardy including a false police report and/or a frivolous lawsuit, doxxing, swatting, false comments and/or malicious comments using threatening words or phrases, defamation or libel or slander, disparagement or other reputational harm to the good business reputation of the company or its digital solutions and digital technologies, commission of any crimes against the company, commission of any torts against the company, impersonate the company, or attempts to commit any fraudulent activities against the company. A threat against the company may also take the form of publishing a threat against the company onto and through any posting of threatening information on any news website, social media platform or website, in emails, text messages, any bot, robot, chatbot, or any other form of media and communication technology. Threats may be started from any location on the internet or from any geographic location in the world. Please see Washington State Law - RCW 9A.46.020.

**Tort** - an action resulting in harm to persons, property, business relationships or financial/economic interests, that is classified as a civil wrong caused by the breach of any legal duty or duties that the law imposes on persons or entities that have some relationship to each other, but that is a harm that is not the same as a breach of a contract.

This license agreement may be issued to any market of end-users, governing the use of digital electronic products, services, data, apps, software, and other technologies, by many end-users and made available for free during a limited time to any public market.

**Troll, Trolling** - speech in any form or format online, on the internet, in email, in text messages, or on social media, that contains words, phrases, symbols and imagery that are individually or altogether: abusive, attacking, accusatory, malicious, confrontational, taunting, baiting, lying, provoking, griefing, spamming, deceitful, fraudulent, insulting, hateful, hostile, harassing, bullying, punishing, exploitative, manipulative, misleading, malevolent, threatening, illegal, sabotaging, fighting words to provoke a fight, defamatory and/or libelous, incendiary, deliberately containing false information, and/or false accusations. Trolling speech deliberately and recklessly disregards truth and verifiable facts and instead, uses words and phrases that are intended to cause: harm, anger, rage, chaos, disruption, social unrest, cancelation of a person's membership in a social group or enjoyment of their good reputation, incitement to an illegal act, incitement to violence, and overall it is speech that seeks to target in a negative and hurtful way any person, place or thing with a goal of showing harm, diminishment, disrepute, disruptions, delays, and/or actual destruction of a person, place, or thing. Often the intention of a troll that actively engages in trolling someone (or some entity, i.e. a business entity), is to cause the permanent loss of something beneficial that is used or is enjoyed as a legal right of use, and is affected by or through the use of the internet, use of a social media platform, or use of another type of communication through any technology (emails, text messages), or access to and use of any marketplace and online marketplace. Any troll's hate speech may cause loss or destruction to a person's reputation, social standing, market position, or membership in any social group, and the victim of trolling often suffers financial losses and business opportunity losses directly or indirectly caused by an internet troll's hate speech that was published on the internet, through messages, or was published on social media. In the pursuit of a perverse goal to cause irreparable harm a troll's hate speech may also aim to cause the harms of a person or entity suffering from the expressed hatred, contempt, ridicule, or other types of damage (i.e. financial losses) from other people in society, participants in a marketplace, or from others online avoiding, abandoning, expelling, refusing to do business with, or canceling a person or entity. A troll's hate speech may also be directed toward a group of persons or entities.

"Usage" means a well-known, widespread, customary and/or uniformly applied practice. "Adverse Use" means any use without the user having a license or permission. (See also, the definitions of: "actual use," and "adverse use," and "fraudulent use," and "intended use," and "scope of use").

**User Credentials** - any end-user's authorized and secure alpha-numeric text code, symbols, keys, passwords, passcodes, or other information, communicated from a company or person to an end-user, consumer, customer, or other person, that establishes a more secure connection to any service, resource, system, network, app, webpage, email, message, or other electronic resource, or that allows access, passage, use, or completion of a transaction, message, communication, or other exchange of electronic information.

**Username** - a unique account holder name, (used simultaneously with a password, passkey, or other sign-in encryption codes), used to sign into a computer resource, website, web application, software, technology, platform, hub, online bank account, or other online digital resource available over a network, the internet, or worldwide web. A username is often made of specific alphanumeric characters and symbols in a unique sequence. Sometimes a username can be an email address, or a PIN code.

**Utah Consumer Privacy Act - ( UCPA )** - text of Utah S.B. 227 Consumer Privacy Act available at this weblink:  [UCPA - Utah Consumer Privacy Act](https://le.utah.gov/~2022/bills/static/SB0227.html "UCPA - Utah Consumer Privacy Act").

**V.A.T.** - value added tax, imposed on goods, property, and services, by a taxing authority. Other examples of V.A.T. related taxes (in Canada) are: G.S.T., H.S.T., P.S.T., Q.S.T., R.S.T.

**Valid License** - a license that is legally sufficient to be binding upon the parties to the license.

**Variable Costs** - charges or payments given in exchange for goods or services which varies in quantity along with some quantity of use, consumption, or transaction amount. Please also see "Costs," "Fixed Costs," "Recurring Costs," and "Other Costs" in these definitions.

**Variable Fees** - charges or payments given in exchange for goods or services which varies in quantity along with some quantity of use, consumption, or transaction amount. Please also see "Fees," "Fixed Fees," "Recurring Fees," "Other Fees" and "Late Fees" in these definitions.

**Variable Prices** - charges or payments given in exchange for goods or services which varies in quantity along with some quantity of use, consumption, or transaction amount. Please also see "Prices," "Fixed Prices," "Recurring Prices," and "Other Prices" in these definitions.

**Venue** - in the U.S.A., venue refers to the _location_ within a State, i.e., a county, parish, or borough, where any legal case and/or legal dispute is scheduled to be heard in a court of law or heard by a court approved arbitrator.

**Verification Code** - any alpha-numeric text code, symbols, keys, passwords, passcodes, or other information, communicated from a company or person to an end-user, consumer, customer, or other person, that establishes a more secure connection to any service, resource, system, network, app, webpage, email, message, or other electronic resource, or that allows access, passage, use, or completion of a transaction, message, communication, or other exchange of electronic information.

**Verification Credentials** - any authorized and secure alpha-numeric text code, symbols, keys, passwords, passcodes, or other information, communicated from a company or person to an end-user, consumer, customer, or other person, that establishes a more secure connection to any service, resource, system, network, app, webpage, email, message, or other electronic resource, or that allows access, passage, use, or completion of a transaction, message, communication, or other exchange of electronic information.
