**Verify Account Holder** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of a company created account for any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Bank Account** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of a bank account, credit account, credit-union account, or any other type of account at any financial institution for any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Bank Card** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of a bank card issued by a bank, creditor, credit-union, or any financial card issued by any other type of financial institution for any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Business Owner** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of a business owner, ownership, or holder of a beneficial interest in any business entity of any kind.

**Verify Contact Information** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any information used to communicate with and contact any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Credential** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any credential, or related information to prove the identity, account, user permissions, access, transactions, communications, or any other electronic information of any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Entity** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any entity that is not a natural person, including without limitation: ownership, management, employees, or beneficiaries of any entity of any kind.

**Verify ID - Verify I.D.** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any identification ("ID") credentials, or related information to prove the identity, account, user permissions, access, transactions, communications, or any other electronic information of any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Identity** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any identification ("ID") credentials, or related information to prove the identity, account, user permissions, access, transactions, communications, or any other electronic information of any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Payment Source** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any payment sources, origins, authorizations, and/or the initiation and request at the point of origin in a financial system for any payment related transactions outside of the company whereby money is sent to the company in exchange for goods and services that are accessed, viewed, received, or used in any way by any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Verify Payment** - efforts and actions involving the use of independent factual data to prove the truth, accuracy, or validity of any payments and related transactions whereby money is sent to the company in exchange for goods and services that are accessed, viewed, received, or used in any way by any person, entity, end-user, customer, or consumer.

**Version** - a name, number, date, symbol, or other designation, showing a distinctive and unique identification of what digital solution or digital technology is, which edition, which iteration, which sequence, and which creation date, time, place, that it was completed, published, or distributed to a public marketplace of end-user consumers. Please also see the definitions of "upgrade," "downgrade."

**Video** - visual images in motion and sounds that are recorded onto media that can be displayed, viewed by humans, and replayed.

**Violate, Violation** - a breaking of a law, rule, policy, regulation, rule: a breach of a law or of a code of behavior that is required to be considered lawful, law abiding, or an action that is in conformity with a rule, policy, regulation, and law.

**Violation of Contract ( Breach of Contract )** - the failure to perform fully a contractual duty when it is due is a breach of contract. In the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements of this company, one example of a breach includes (without limitation); default, non-payment of billed invoice for digital solutions and digital technologies delivered to consumers. A “material breach” is a breach that is serious enough to justify the other party in abandoning the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements. A “material breach” is one that substantially defeats the purpose of the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements, or relates to an essential element of the contracts, terms of use agreements, and license agreements, and deprives the injured party of a benefit that he or she or they would have reasonably expected to occur.

**Violation of Copyright ( Copyright Infringement )** - any action that interferes unlawfully with the exclusive rights of the copyright owner.

**Violation of Data Use** - any action that interferes unlawfully, breaches, misuses, or breaks any of the exclusive rights and/or requirements of the terms and conditions of any data use agreement, license, service contract, or legal requirement relating to data.

**Violation of Law** - any infraction, disobedience, non-compliance, or breaking of, any law.

**Violation of License** - any action that interferes unlawfully, breaches, misuses, or breaks any of the exclusive rights and/or requirements of the terms and conditions of a valid license.

**Violation of Trademark ( Trademark Infringement )** - any action that interferes unlawfully, breaches, or breaks any of the exclusive rights of the trademark owner.

**Virginia Consumer Data Privacy Law** - [Chapter 53 Consumer Data Protection Act § 59.1-575](https://law.lis.virginia.gov/vacodefull/title59.1/chapter53/ "Virginia Chapter 53 Consumer Data Protection Act § 59.1-575")

**VLLM Very Large Language Model** -

**Vishing** - voice phishing that uses voice communication to try and trick a consumer into giving up sensitive information: it is also a type of cyberattack.

**Voice Inputs** -

**Void** - a transaction, rule, policy, law, requirement, request, offer, acceptance, payment, promise, debt, or any other thing, which has been cancelled, nullified, stopped, retracted, withdrawn, repudiated, renounced, disclaimed, or otherwise ceased. The consequence and result of something being void is that it has no legal existence or legal requirement to be performed, fulfilled, delivered, paid, acted upon, or complied with.

**WAF - W.A.F.** - web application firewall. Please click on this weblink:  [explanation of a web application firewall at cloudflare.com](https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ddos/glossary/web-application-firewall-waf/ "explanation of a web application firewall at cloudflare.com").

**WAF Restrictions, W.A.F. Restrictions** - any rule or limit that may block any end-user, consumer, or customer from using a website of the company. Restrictions also refer to any web application firewall rules, codes, traffic comparison database lookups, or other cybersecurity digital inspections of digital computer communications of end-users, consumers, and customers, when they request information from and/or file access to any HTTP or HTTPS servers, company websites, and web applications. The automated electronic web application firewall is a software program designed to prevent malicious users from getting to the company network servers and web applications. The company uses website user data inspection, lookup matching, and if necessary, then immediately apply blocking of any use of network/website/server access to any user for potential or actual violations of cybersecurity rules. Cybersecurity rules are pre-programmed into a web application firewall. WAF cybersecurity rules may evaluate an end-users' country of origin, IP address, ASN, number of computer access requests, and other malicious user network traffic patterns. WAF restrictions are designed to keep the HTTP and/or HTTPS server and its information safe from malicious hacking and to prevent cybersecurity risks being used against the company from unauthorized users' attempts to get access to the computer server, disrupt communications, steal data, and/or make unauthorized changes to the server contents and/or interfere with and disrupt the lawful and safe operations of network servers and web applications.

**WAN - W.A.N.** - wide area network. Several computers in different physical locations over a large geographic area (wide area) which are connected by an electronic digital network.

**Warranty** - a promise or guarantee that a product will function and work as specified and is free from significant defects.

**Warranty of Fitness for a Particular Purpose** - in a sale of goods, ( where the Uniform Commercial Code U.C.C. § 2-315 would apply to the transaction(s)), the seller is aware of the buyer's specific intended use and purpose of the goods to be sold. Warranties can be disclaimed (UCC §2-316(2)).

**WASM - W.A.S.M.** - WebAssembly (abbreviated Wasm) is a binary instruction format for a stack-based virtual machine. Wasm is designed as a portable compilation target for programming languages, enabling deployment on the web for client and server applications. Please see "Web Assembly" in these definitions.  [https://webassembly.org/](https://webassembly.org/ "wasm - web assembly - https://webassembly.org/").

**Watermark - Digital Watermark** - image, text, or any other symbol that is transparent and appear as super-imposed over a document, digital document, image, digital image, or other digital information, which identifies the true creator, brand name, copyright, trademark, or other identifying information.

**Web Assembly - ( WASM - W.A.S.M. )** - WebAssembly (abbreviated Wasm) is a binary instruction format for a stack-based virtual machine. Wasm is designed as a portable compilation target for programming languages, enabling deployment on the web for client and server applications.  [https://webassembly.org/](https://webassembly.org/ "wasm - web assembly - https://webassembly.org/").

**Web Only Platform** - any collection of computer technologies, cloud computer, web information, and web specific software altogether used to create and provide web services, features, functions, information, and technology to consumers. The phrase "web platform" describes technology selections used to create a website or webservice, as in: what technologies do you use in your web platform? It also means any technology or technologies offered and used as a destination and source to host or provide any type of technology service, (located on or through the internet & world-wide-web) such as: cloud-based web applications, or a computer network servers: any complete web based cloud technology platform used for cloud-based apps and cloud-enabled enterprise applications. A web only platform is different than an intranet based platform, or a local area network based platform of apps and technology services.

**Web Page** - any electronic document written in hyper-text-markup-language ("HTML") or any other web computer language, and/or files, which is posted onto the world-wide-web, the internet, or an intranet within a company, association, organization, or other entity.

**Web Platform** - any collection of computer technologies, cloud computer, web information, and web specific software altogether used to create and provide web services, features, functions, information, and technology to consumers. The phrase "web platform" describes technology selections used to create a website or webservice, as in: what technologies do you use in your web platform?

**Web Portal** - a web page or website that presents a variety of electronic information in a format that is focused upon and relevant to the interests of a specific target market of consumers. While a web platform describes technologies used to create a website or webservice, it is different from a web portal, which describes specific information on a website for a specific target market audience of consumers.

**Webhook** - an electronic message sent automatically to a digital device from a software application, web application, website, or other digital technology, when an electronic data even occurs.

**Website** - a specific IP-internet-protocol address with a specific U.R.L. that is the destination location on any network that hosts, displays, and communicates a collection of any electronic documents written in hyper-text-markup-language ("HTML") or any other web computer language, and/or files, that is posted onto the world-wide-web, the internet, or an intranet within a company, association, organization, or other entity.

**Weekly** - a time interval of something occurring once each seven (7) days, often a term used to describe recurring transactions over multiple days which a consumer pays for every week, as in a recurring weekly paid subscription for seven (7) days of service.

**WiFi - Wi-Fi** - a communication protocol to allow digital devices and computers to communicate electronically with each other over radio waves (wireless) and interconnect to a wireless local area network, allowing additional connections to the internet and world wide web. Wi-Fi is a communication protocol defined by standards of the Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers ("IEEE"). Several types of Wi-Fi exist, differing by frequency and speed, as listed in the standard [IEEE 802.11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IEEE_802.11 "IEEE 802.11 WiFi").

**Willful** - any voluntary action involving a conscious awareness that an action is illegal, has a malevolent purpose, or involves any legally inexcusable carelessness.

**Wire Fraud** - violation of U.S. Federal Law - an act of fraud by using electronic interstate communications device(s) in order to make false representations and/or false promises in order to unlawfully get money, property, or honest services (18 USC section 1343 through section 1349). Some examples include attempts to cheat and defraud a person out of their money through computer malware, phishing scams, email scams, text message scams, threatening phone calls.

**Withdraw, Withdraw Offer (contract)** - taking back, removing, canceling, taking away something. "Withdrawing an offer" when negotiating a new contract refers to the action of canceling an offer. A withdrawal is often communicated in a written format to give notice of cancelation and to establish a specific data and time that the notice was given.

**Without Authorization** - “without authorization” is the act of accessing a protected computer without permission or authorization, see the Computer Fraud and Abuse Act (“CFAA”), at 18 U.S.C. §§ 1030(a)(1), (a)(2), (a)(3), (a)(4), and (a)(5)(B)-(C).

**Write (to a computer file)** - the electronic action of adding data to an electronic computer file and then saving the file so that the data is stored in that file. Writing data to a file changes the file's data contents. Writing to a computer file is the same thing as recording new data and saving it electronically into a file. The electronic action of saving an electronic file will often change several characteristics of the file, including (without limitation): the data contents, the file size, dates, and times of the file's most recent "save" operations, and any other file settings selected by the end-user creating, changing, updating, or deleting the file (read permissions, encryption, file location).

**WWW** - (world wide web) -the world wide web is commonly referred to as WWW, W3, or the Web—is a system of interconnected public webpages accessible through the Internet. The Web is not the same as the Internet. The Web is one of many applications built on top of the Internet. [https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/World\_Wide\_Web](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/World_Wide_Web "Mozilla definition of WWW")

**X3-DH/ECDH Ratchet** - end-to-end encryption of electronic digital communications by using specific protocols and algorithms. Please see weblinks:  [Double Ratchet encryption as used by Signal.org](https://signal.org/docs/specifications/doubleratchet/ "Double Ratchet encryption as used by Signal.org")  [Double Ratchet Algorithm - summary at wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_Ratchet_Algorithm "Double Ratchet Algorithm - summary at wikipedia.org").

**XAAS - X.A.A.S** - "anything as a service" (XaaS) of cloud computing services available to consumers.

**Yearly** - a time interval of something occurring once each twelve-months (12 months), often a term used to describe recurring transactions over multiple years which a consumer pays for every twelve-months, as in a recurring yearly paid subscription for twelve-months of service.

**You** - the word "you" refers to the "consumer," which means any person or entity that uses any solutions, services or products created or provided by aixeno inc. A "consumer" includes (without limitation), any persons, and entities commonly referred to as: businesses, non-profits, governments, non-government organizations, charitable organizations, educational institutions, and scientific organizations.

**Your Account** - an account already set up with the company that contains personally identifiable information of a single client, customer, person, or entity. An "account" is a record of information at any point(s) in time showing interactions and transactions between any parties, persons, customers, providers, businesses, other entities, where the parties' information is quantifiable and records the amount(s) of transactions, business dealings, money amounts, subscriptions, investments, financial transactions, assets, liabilities, equities, revenues, expenses, information, data, exchanges of anything of value, property, identifying information, stored information, or any other thing that can be recorded or described or explained. An account may be in any form or format, electronic or otherwise.

**Your Payment** - any payment(s) made to the company from any customer, client, or end-user: the word "your" refers to the customer, client, or end-user making a payment.

**Your Payment Has Been Accepted** - a payment attempted by a customer, client, or end-user, and the payment was completed successfully.

**Your Payment Has Been Placed On Hold** - a payment attempted by a customer, client, or end-user, yet the payment is temporarily paused, put on hold, frozen, or otherwise interrupted during a transaction processing step for any of several possible reasons: verification of identity, verification of sufficient funds in the payment account, verification of card information, verification of account information and/or spending limits, verification of legal authorization for payment on account, approval needed by the payment processor, approval required by the bank, or for any other reason.

**Your Payment Has Been Rejected** - a payment attempted by a customer, client, or end-user, yet the payment was declined, rejected, or refused, for any of several possible reasons: insufficient funds in the payment account, card expired, account expired, account information is incorrect, card information is incorrect, declined by the payment processor, declined by the bank, or for any other reason.

**ZTN - Z.T.N. - Zero Trust Network** - "strict identity verification for every person and device trying to access resources on a private network, regardless of whether they are sitting within or outside of the network perimeter"  [see Cloudflare definition of ZTN](https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/glossary/what-is-zero-trust/ "Cloudflare definition of ZTN")

**ZTNA** - zero trust network access: please see definition of "ZTN - zero trust network" in the definitions above.
